{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01RxqxYtaQW9V2mufsr6Q7qZ","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"85: //\\n86: // BytecodeEmitter receives an AST, and utilizes helper classes to generate the\\n87: // bytecode sequence, and related stencil data.\\n88: //\\n89: // BytecodeEmitter can be nested, in order to emit inner non-lazy function\\n90: // scripts.\\n91: //\\n92: //\\n93: // Bytecode structures\\n94: // -------------------\\n95: //\\n96: // While bytecode is being emitted, it is separated into 2 parts, the prologue\\n97: // and the main part.  The prologue part contains instantiation of the declared\\n98: // variables, functions, and special names in function.  The main part contains\\n99: // the remaining part of the bytecode.\\n100: //\\n101: // The generated bytecode is stored into the following 2 classes, before\\n102: // converting them into stencil data (See ImmutableScriptData and\\n103: // BytecodeEmitter::createImmutableScriptData):\\n104: //\\n105: //   * BytecodeSection\\n106: //   * PerScriptData\\n107: //\\n108: // BytecodeSection stores the bytecode sequence and data directly associated\\n109: // with opcode or index inside the bytecode sequence.\\n110: //\\n111: // PerScriptData contains data referred from the bytecode, that is mostly the\\n112: // list of GC things.\\n113: //\\n114: //\\n115: // Bindings\\n116: // --------\\n117: //\\n118: // # Scope and bindings\\n119: //\\n120: // When emitting AST node that's associated with a given scope, EmitterScope is\\n121: // allocated to store/cache the bindings information.\\n122: //\\n123: // This information is used when emitting an opcode that accesses bindings, to\\n124: // determine where the binding is stored, and how the binding should be\\n125: // accessed, including which opcode to use and what operand to use for it.\\n126: //\\n127: //\\n128: // # Temporal Dead Zone (TDZ) check cache\\n129: //\\n130: // The spec requires TDZ check for all lexical variable access, but emitting\\n131: // TDZ check for all operation increases the bytecode size and affects the\\n132: // performance.  TDZCheckCache is a cache to optimize away unnecessary TDZ check\\n133: // operations.\\n134: //\\n135: // See comments for TDZCheckCache for more details.\\n136: //\\n137: //\\n138: // Control structures\\n139: // ------------------\\n140: //\\n141: // # Jump list\\n142: //\\n143: // When emitting jump-related bytecode (if-else, break/continue, try-catch),\\n144: // forward jump is tracked by JumpList class, in order to patch the jump\\n145: // after the jump target is emitted.\\n146: //\\n147: // See the comment above JumpList class for mode details.\\n148: //\\n149: //\\n150: // # Loop and label\\n151: //\\n152: // Control structure related to break/continue is handled by NestableControl and\\n153: // its subclasses.  Those classes handle jump with labelled and un-labelled\\n154: // break/continue, stack balancing around them, TDZ check cache for the\\n155: // loop's basic block, and association between the control and the scope.\\n156: //\\n157: //\\n158: // Emitter helpers\\n159: // ---------------\\n160: //\\n161: // Bytecode sequence or structure specific to certain syntax (e.g. if, for, try)\\n162: // are handled by emitter helper classes.\\n163: //\\n164: // Each emitter helper is defined in *Emitter.{cpp,h} in this directory.\\n165: //\\n166: // Emitter helpers should meet the following requirements:\\n167: //   * helper classes should be ParseNode-agnostic\\n168: //   * helper classes shouldn't contain `JS::Rooted` field, given they can be\\n169: //     held in `mozilla::Maybe` in the consumer or other helper classes\\n170: //   * instantiation (ctor/dtor) of the emitter helper class shouldn't\\n171: //     modify BytecodeEmitter, except for nestable controls\\n172: //   * instantiation (ctor/dtor) of the emitter helper class shouldn't\\n173: //     read BytecodeEmitter field that can change before the first method call.\\n174: //     Such data should be explicitly passed as parameter, or be accessed inside\\n175: //     the method\\n176: //   * methods that emits bytecode should be named `emit*` or `prepareFor*`\\n177: //   * methods and their names shouldn't require the consumer knowing the\\n178: //     details of the bytecode sequence/structure that the helper emits\\n179: //     * implicit branch or scope/control handling should be hidden from here\\n193: //       helper.deallocateScopeForB();\\n194: //       helper.emitJumpTarget();\\n195: //\\n196: //       // Good!\\n197: //       helper.prepareForA();\\n198: //       ... // emit bytecode for A here\\n199: //       helper.prepareForB();\\n200: //       ... // emit bytecode for B here\\n201: //       helper.emitEnd();\\n202: //   * helper classes should track state transition and assert it in each\\n203: //     method call, to avoid misuse\\n204: //   * it's recommended to defer receiving parameter until the parameter value\\n205: //     is actually used in the method, instead of receiving and storing them\\n206: //     into instance fields\\n207: //\\n208: // See comment block above each helper class for more details and example usage.\\n209: \\n210: struct Certain limitations of\\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\\n28:  *\\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\\n30:  *\\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\\n33:  * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\\n34:  * ParserBase type below.\\n35:  *\\n36:  * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\\n37:  *\\n38:  * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\\n39:  * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\\n47:  * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\\n48:  * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\\n49:  *\\n50:  * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\\n53:  * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\\n54:  * to \\\"create an arguments object for a function\\\" obviously varies between\\n55:  * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\\n56:  * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\\n57:  * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\\n58:  *\\n59:  * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\\n60:  * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\\n61:  * further below).\\n62:  *\\n63:  * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\\n66:  * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\\n67:  *\\n68:  *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\\n69:  *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\\n70:  *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\\n71:  *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\\n72:  *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\\n73:  *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\\n74:  *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\\n75:  *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\\n76:  *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\\n77:  *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\\n78:  *     character type.\\n79:  *\\n80:  * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\\n81: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-80\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"496a47e8-6934-43e8-bfd9-e3da2e05e606","uuid":"9ed590f4-9d50-42f4-8806-fe1162dac37b","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C++; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sts=2 et sw=2 tw=80:\\n3:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\\n4:  * License, v. 2.0. Certain limitations of\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\n28:  *\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\n30:  *\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\n33:  * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\n34:  * ParserBase type below.\n35:  *\n36:  * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\n37:  *\n38:  * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\n39:  * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\n41:  *\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Wq9MfWM7Cm4dKf4Bt9MnLo","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C++; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sts=2 et sw=2 tw=80:\\n3:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\\n4:  * License, v. 2.0. If a copy of the MPL was not distributed with this\\n5:  * file, You can obtain one at http://mozilla.org/MPL/2.0/. */\\n6: \\n7: /*\\n8:  * Streaming access to the raw tokens of JavaScript source.\\n9:  *\\n10:  * Because JS tokenization is context-sensitive -- a '/' could be either a\\n11:  * regular expression *or* a division operator depending on context -- the\\n12:  * various token stream classes are mostly not useful outside of the Parser\\n13:  * where they reside.  We should probably eventually merge the two concepts.\\n14:  */\\n15: #ifndef frontend_TokenStream_h\\n16: #define frontend_TokenStream_h\\n17: \\n18: /*\\n19:  * [SMDOC] Parser Token Stream\\n20:  *\\n21:  * A token stream exposes the raw tokens -- operators, names, numbers,\\n22:  * keywords, and so on -- of JavaScript source code.\\n23:  *\\n24:  * These are the components of the overall token stream concept:\\n25:  * TokenStreamShared, TokenStreamAnyChars, TokenStreamCharsBase<Unit>,\\n26:  * TokenStreamChars<Unit>, and TokenStreamSpecific<Unit, AnyCharsAccess>.\\n27:  *\\n28:  * == TokenStreamShared → ∅ ==\\n29:  *\\n30:  * Certain aspects of tokenizing are used everywhere:\\n31:  *\\n32:  *   * modifiers (used to select which context-sensitive interpretation of a\\n33:  *     character should be used to decide what token it is) and modifier\\n34:  *     assertion handling;\\n35:  *   * flags on the overall stream (have we encountered any characters on this\\n36:  *     line?  have we hit a syntax error?  and so on);\\n37:  *   * and certain token-count constants.\\n38:  *\\n39:  * These are all defined in TokenStreamShared.  (They could be namespace-\\n40:  * scoped, but it seems tentatively better not to clutter the namespace.)\\n41:  *\\n42:  * == TokenStreamAnyChars → TokenStreamShared ==\\n43:  *\\n44:  * Certain aspects of tokenizing have meaning independent of the character type\\n45:  * of the source text being tokenized: line/column number information, tokens\\n46:  * in lookahead from determining the meaning of a prior token, compilation\\n47:  * options, the filename, flags, source map URL, access to details of the\\n48:  * current and next tokens (is the token of the given type?  what name or\\n49:  * number is contained in the token?  and other queries), and others.\\n50:  *\\n51:  * All this data/functionality *could* be duplicated for both single-byte and\\n52:  * double-byte tokenizing, but there are two problems.  First, it's potentially\\n53:  * wasteful if the compiler doesnt recognize it can unify the concepts.  (And\\n54:  * if any-character concepts are intermixed with character-specific concepts,\\n55:  * potentially the compiler *can't* unify them because offsets into the\\n56:  * hypothetical TokenStream<Unit>s would differ.)  Second, some of this stuff\\n57:  * needs to be accessible in ParserBase, the aspects of JS language parsing\\n58:  * that have meaning independent of the character type of the source text being\\n59:  * parsed. They're split\\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \\\"use strict\\\" code. The \\\"use strict\\\" bit is stored in\\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\\n48:  *\\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\\n50:  * different groups of flags:\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \\\"passed down\\\"\\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"are we parsing strict code?\\\", and so\\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\\n57:  * \\\"returned up\\\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"did we see a use strict\\n58:  * directive\\\"?\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\\n63:  *\\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\\n67:  * can be optimized away.\\n68:  *\\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\\n80:  *\\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \\\"pass-down\\\"\\n84:  * data and some \\\"return-up\\\" data.\\n85:  *\\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\\n90:  *\\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\\n93:  *\\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\\n96:  *\\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\\n99:  *\\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\\n103:  */\\n104: \\n105: class JSFunction;\\n106: class JSObject;\\n107: class JSScript;\\n108: struct
